INDIAN COMMERCIAL DIRECTORY a prominent part in the Society were the late Mr. Kalanji Gopalji, who supervised and collected the rent of the cottages belonging to the Society until the time of his death, and also the late Mr. A. L. Billomoria, who contributed very liberally to all the funds and held a responsible position in the Society. The aim of the Society is the upliftment of the members in cultural and religious fields, to further the national cause of the Motherland and National Institutions. The Society was also represented on the Transvaal British Indian Association. The following are some of the many activities of the Society -— The Society, represented by the late Mr. Parshottam Vallabh Bhagat (CAaiyman) and Mr. Prag Prema (Secretary), was a signatory to the illuminated Address presented to Mr. Polak by the Transvaal British Indian Association. The Society also assisted The British Indian Association financially and morally. A substantial donation to the Patidar Boarding House at Surat (India) on an undertaking being given by Mr. Vithalbhai Mehta, that the students of every community would be permitted to reside in the Boarding House. A donation of approximately £200 to assist the erection of a Dharmashala at Unai, a sacred place in India, This provides accommodation for the pilgrims of the community. A present of £20 which was given to Mr. Narcndas Vithaldas Damania, in appreciation for the services he rendered to the Hindoo Community by erecting a Hindoo Crematorium in Johannesburg. The Hindoo Crematorium was equipped with the necessary furniture by the Society. A donation of £37 10s. Od. to the Orrisa Famine Fund. (India.) A donation of £37 10s. 0d. for the relief of the victims of the Jalianwala Bag (India) (through Mahatmaji) A donation of £135 to the Tilak Swaraj Fund (through Mahatmaji). A donation of a purse of £50 to Pandit Ishverdatta Vidyalankara. (Gurukur Kangari.) The purchase of a Stand for the sum of £250 in the 12th Street, Vrededorp, Johannesburg. It was mainly through the efforts of tbe Society that Mr. Dalpatram Vanmalibhai Darji arrived from India as an educated immigrant. A donation of a purse of £26 5s. Od. to Mr. Shastriji for the Servant of India Society. In the year 1927, the Society decided to erect a Hall on the Vrededorp Stand, and although the members contributed to this fund very liberally, it was later argued by some of the members that cottages should be erected on the Stand. Thus a dispute arose in the Community, and the Society ceased functioning until 1933. However, thanks to the efforts of Mr. Govindbhai Chbibabhai, the Society then again started to function, and since then its activities were as follows :— A Draft of £49 3s. Od. was sent to Babu Rajendraprasad, Patna (India) for the relief of the victims of the earthquake in Bihar. In the year 1936 the Society decided to erect cottages on the Stand, and members contributed approxi- mately £900 towards this fund. At present the Society owns four cottages, and has utilised one of the cottages for the purpose of a Hall. Numerous meetings and other functions have been held in this Hall, which has been a tremendous asset to the Community. The cottages are let and are thus a source of income to the Fund. The Society last year founded a library known as the Transvaal Darjee Mandal Library, which is, and will be of great educational value and interest to the whole community. The library is housed in the Hall. The Society has granted a scholarship of three hundred and eighty-seven rupees to Mr. D. M. Dalal, who is doing his M.A. Class at St. Kavier’s College, Bombay. A sum of approximately £115 was collected from the members and handed over to the Lourenco Marques Bharat Samaj. The Society is also trying to discourage those old traditions and empty shibboleths in social matters which retard the progress of the community. The Society has completely justified its existence, playing as it does an important and valuable part in the cultural life of the Community. Through its charitable and honest works it enjoys the confidence and respect of those whom it serves. 73a.

BOX 10 LOURENCO MARQUES (THE INDIAN MOHAMEDAN COMMUNITY), AT LOURENCO MARQUES The photo is of. the Muslim School to be erected at a cost of £4,000, and another £8,000 will be spent towards maintenance of the school. by building shops for revenue purposes. Originally started in 1934, the new school will be the fruit of many years of labour of the Muslim Community of Lourenco Marques. An income derived from investments of £150 per menth will be spent towards education. P.O. Box 435 Telephone 1032 Tel. Add. “AKA” Code: A.B.C. 6th Edition Fabrica Nacional de Velas Proprietors: N.S. GUJRAL and RAJPARA) The languages taught will be Arabic, Urdu, Portuguese, English and Gujarati. Portuguese will be compulsory. Jn addition, on the top of the shops, there will be a library hall and a Musafarkhana, particularly for the use of passengers from the Union and Mocambique Colony. Out of £12,000 necessary, £6,000 has been already donated by the people of Lourenco Marques, Gaza and Inhambane district. To complete the amount « committee of the following is formed: Abdool Sacoor Abdul Latif & Co., Aboobakar Abdul Rehman & Co.. Hassam Adam & Co., Essa Moossa & Co., Adam Seedat & Co. and Kassam Adam.
